     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dartmouth_College&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Dartmouth_Big_Green" title="Dartmouth Big Green">Dartmouth Big Green</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Darthmouth_vs_Princeton_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Darthmouth_vs_Princeton_1.jpg/220px-Darthmouth_vs_Princeton_1.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Darthmouth_vs_Princeton_1.jpg/330px-Darthmouth_vs_Princeton_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Darthmouth_vs_Princeton_1.jpg/440px-Darthmouth_vs_Princeton_1.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Darthmouth_vs_Princeton_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> A Dartmouth varsity hockey game against Princeton at 
        <a href="/wiki/Thompson_Arena" title="Thompson Arena">Thompson Arena</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Approximately 20% of students participate in a varsity sport, and nearly 80% participate in some form of club, varsity, intramural, or other athletics.<sup id="cite_ref-What_percentage_of_Dartmouth_students_play_a_varsity_sport.3F_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-What_percentage_of_Dartmouth_students_play_a_varsity_sport.3F-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2007, Dartmouth College fielded 34 intercollegiate varsity teams: 16 for men, 16 for women, and coeducational sailing and equestrian programs. Dartmouth's athletic teams compete in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">National Collegiate Athletic Association</a> (NCAA) <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a> eight-member <a href="/wiki/Ivy_League" title="Ivy League">Ivy League</a> conference; some teams also participate in the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_College_Athletic_Conference" title="Eastern College Athletic Conference">Eastern College Athletic Conference</a> (ECAC).<sup id="cite_ref-about-dartmouth-athletics_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-about-dartmouth-athletics-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> As is mandatory for the members of the Ivy League, Dartmouth College does not offer athletic scholarships.<sup id="cite_ref-about-dartmouth-athletics_136-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-about-dartmouth-athletics-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-What_is_the_Ivy_League.3F_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-What_is_the_Ivy_League.3F-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition to the traditional American team sports (football, basketball, baseball, and ice hockey), Dartmouth competes at the varsity level in many other sports including track and field, sailing, tennis, rowing, soccer, skiing, and lacrosse.<sup id="cite_ref-about-dartmouth-facts_8-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-about-dartmouth-facts-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The College also offers 26 club and intramural sports such as rugby, water polo, figure skating, boxing, volleyball, ultimate frisbee, and cricket, leading to a 75% participation rate in athletics among the undergraduate student body.<sup id="cite_ref-about-dartmouth-facts_8-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-about-dartmouth-facts-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Club_Sports_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Club_Sports-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> The Dartmouth Men's Rugby Team, founded in 1951, has also been ranked among the best collegiate teams in that sport over many years. The figure skating team won the national championship five straight times from 2004 through 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-Dartmouth_Wins_Fourth_Consecutive_National_Title_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dartmouth_Wins_Fourth_Consecutive_National_Title-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition to the academic requirements for graduation, Dartmouth requires every undergraduate to complete a 50-yard (46&nbsp;m) swim and three terms of physical education.<sup id="cite_ref-General_Academic_Requirements_for_Graduation_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-General_Academic_Requirements_for_Graduation-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Technology">Technology</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dartmouth_College&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Technology">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Dartmouth_College_campus_2007-09-24_Baker-Berry_Library_02.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Dartmouth_College_campus_2007-09-24_Baker-Berry_Library_02.JPG/220px-Dartmouth_College_campus_2007-09-24_Baker-Berry_Library_02.JPG" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Dartmouth_College_campus_2007-09-24_Baker-Berry_Library_02.JPG/330px-Dartmouth_College_campus_2007-09-24_Baker-Berry_Library_02.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Dartmouth_College_campus_2007-09-24_Baker-Berry_Library_02.JPG/440px-Dartmouth_College_campus_2007-09-24_Baker-Berry_Library_02.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Dartmouth_College_campus_2007-09-24_Baker-Berry_Library_02.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Students at a bank of Blitz terminals in Baker-Berry Library.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Technology plays an important role in student life, as Dartmouth has been ranked as one of the most technologically advanced colleges in the world (as in <i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a>'</i>s 2004 ranking of &quot;Hottest for the Tech-Savvy&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-newsweek_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newsweek-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!" title="Yahoo!">Yahoo!</a>'s 1998 &quot;Wired Colleges&quot; list<sup id="cite_ref-About_BlitzMail_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_BlitzMail-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup>). <a href="/wiki/BlitzMail" title="BlitzMail">BlitzMail</a>, the campus <a href="/wiki/E-mail" title="E-mail" class="mw-redirect">e-mail</a> network, plays a tremendous role in social life, as students tend to use it for communication in lieu of <a href="/wiki/Cellular_phones" title="Cellular phones" class="mw-redirect">cellular phones</a> or <a href="/wiki/Instant_messaging" title="Instant messaging">instant messaging</a> programs.<sup id="cite_ref-Cell_phones_make_inroads_on_Blitz-centric_College_campus_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cell_phones_make_inroads_on_Blitz-centric_College_campus-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nyt-blitz_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-blitz-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> Student reliance on BlitzMail (known colloquially as &quot;Blitz,&quot; which functions as both noun and verb<sup id="cite_ref-nyt-blitz_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-blitz-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup>) is reflected by the presence of about 100 public computer terminals intended specifically for BlitzMail use.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt-blitz_144-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-blitz-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> Since 1991, Dartmouth students have been required to own a personal computer.<sup id="cite_ref-Students_required_to_get_wired_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Students_required_to_get_wired-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-All_Students_Required_to_Own_a_Computer_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-All_Students_Required_to_Own_a_Computer-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2001, Dartmouth became the first Ivy League institution to offer entirely ubiquitous wireless internet access.<sup id="cite_ref-newsweek_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newsweek-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> With over 1,400 access points, the network is available throughout all College buildings as well as in most public outdoor spaces.<sup id="cite_ref-Computing_at_Dartmouth_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Computing_at_Dartmouth-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> Other technologies being pioneered include College-wide Video-on-Demand and VoIP rollouts.<sup id="cite_ref-Computing_at_Dartmouth_147-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Computing_at_Dartmouth-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dartmouth_Public_Affairs_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dartmouth_Public_Affairs-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Native_Americans_at_Dartmouth">Native Americans at Dartmouth</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dartmouth_College&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Native Americans at Dartmouth">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>It is often pointed out that the charter of Dartmouth College, granted to <a href="/wiki/Eleazar_Wheelock" title="Eleazar Wheelock">Eleazar Wheelock</a> in 1769, proclaims that the institution was created &quot;for the education and instruction of Youth of the Indian Tribes in this Land in reading, writing and all parts of Learning ... as well as in all liberal Arts and Sciences; and also of English Youth and any others.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-charter_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charter-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> However, Wheelock primarily intended the College to educate white youth and the few Native students that attended Dartmouth experienced much difficulty in an institution ostensibly dedicated to their education. The funds for the Charity School for Native Americans that preceded Dartmouth College were raised primarily by the efforts of a Native American named <a href="/wiki/Samson_Occom" title="Samson Occom">Samson Occom</a>, and at least some of those funds were used to help found the College.<sup id="cite_ref-about-nap_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-about-nap-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The College graduated only 19 Native Americans during its first two hundred years.<sup id="cite_ref-about-nap_149-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-about-nap-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1970, the College established Native American academic and social programs as part of a &quot;new dedication to increasing Native American enrollment.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-about-nap_149-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-about-nap-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup> Since then, Dartmouth has graduated over 700 Native American students from over 200 different tribes, more than the other seven Ivy League universities combined.<sup id="cite_ref-about-nap_149-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-about-nap-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditions">Traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dartmouth_College&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Traditions">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Dartmouth_College_traditions" title="Dartmouth College traditions">Dartmouth College traditions</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:2004_Winter_Carnival_Sculpture.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/2004_Winter_Carnival_Sculpture.JPG/170px-2004_Winter_Carnival_Sculpture.JPG" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/2004_Winter_Carnival_Sculpture.JPG/255px-2004_Winter_Carnival_Sculpture.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/2004_Winter_Carnival_Sculpture.JPG/340px-2004_Winter_Carnival_Sculpture.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:2004_Winter_Carnival_Sculpture.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Snow sculpture at the 2004 Dartmouth Winter Carnival
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Dartmouth is well known for its fierce school spirit and many traditions.<sup id="cite_ref-15th_President_Installed_at_Dartmouth_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15th_President_Installed_at_Dartmouth-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> The College functions on a <a href="/wiki/Academic_term" title="Academic term">quarter system</a>, and one weekend each term is set aside as a traditional celebratory event, known on campus as &quot;big weekends&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-steph_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steph-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Dartmouth_Green:_A_Walking_Tour_of_Dartmouth_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Dartmouth_Green:_A_Walking_Tour_of_Dartmouth-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> or &quot;party weekends&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-Hopkins_Center_offers_many_alternatives_over_weekend_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hopkins_Center_offers_many_alternatives_over_weekend-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup> In the fall term, Homecoming (officially called Dartmouth Night) is marked by a bonfire on the Green constructed by the freshman class.<sup id="cite_ref-homecoming-history_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-homecoming-history-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup> Winter term is celebrated by Winter Carnival, a tradition started in 1911 by the Dartmouth Outing Club to promote winter sports.<sup id="cite_ref-tdr-wc_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tdr-wc-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup> In the spring, Green Key is a weekend mostly devoted to campus parties and celebration.<sup id="cite_ref-Green_Key_History:_Those_Were_the_Days_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Green_Key_History:_Those_Were_the_Days-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The summer term was formerly marked by Tubestock, an unofficial tradition in which the students used wooden rafts and inner tubes to float on the <a href="/wiki/Connecticut_River" title="Connecticut River">Connecticut River</a>. Begun in 1986, Tubestock met its demise in 2006 when Hanover town ordinances and a lack of coherent student protest conspired to defeat the popular tradition.<sup id="cite_ref-Town.2C_College_Weigh_Tubestock_Changes_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Town.2C_College_Weigh_Tubestock_Changes-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> The class of 2008, during their summer term on campus in 2006, replaced the defunct Tubestock with Fieldstock. This new celebration includes a barbecue, live music, and the revival of the 1970s and 1980s tradition of racing homemade chariots around the Green. Unlike Tubestock, Fieldstock is funded and supported by the College.<sup id="cite_ref-Fieldstock.2C_chariots_await_town_approval_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fieldstock.2C_chariots_await_town_approval-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Another longstanding tradition is four-day, student-run <a href="/wiki/Dartmouth_Outing_Club" title="Dartmouth Outing Club">Dartmouth Outing Club</a> trips for incoming freshmen, begun in 1935. Each trip concludes at the <a href="/wiki/Moosilauke_Ravine_Lodge" title="Moosilauke Ravine Lodge">Moosilauke Ravine Lodge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-About_the_Program_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_the_Program-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011, over 96% of freshmen elected to participate.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Insignia_and_other_representations">Insignia and other representations</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dartmouth_College&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Insignia and other representations">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Motto_and_song">Motto and song</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dartmouth_College&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Motto and song">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Dartmouth's motto, chosen by Eleazar Wheelock, is <i>Vox clamantis in deserto</i>. The Latin motto is literally translated as &quot;The voice of one crying in the wilderness&quot;,<sup id="cite_ref-Out_of_the_Woods_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Out_of_the_Woods-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-good_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-good-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup> but is more often rendered as &quot;A voice crying in the wilderness&quot;,<sup id="cite_ref-Daily_Debriefing_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Daily_Debriefing-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup> which attempts to translate the <a href="/wiki/Synecdoche" title="Synecdoche">synecdoche</a> of the phrase. The phrase appears five times in the Bible and is a reference to the college's location on what was once the frontier of European settlement.<sup id="cite_ref-good_161-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-good-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bartlett_Hall.27s_Wheelock_Memorial_Window_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bartlett_Hall.27s_Wheelock_Memorial_Window-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup> Richard Hovey's &quot;<a href="/wiki/Alma_Mater_(Dartmouth_College)" title="Alma Mater (Dartmouth College)">Men of Dartmouth</a>&quot; was elected as the best of Dartmouth's songs in 1896,<sup id="cite_ref-homecoming-history_154-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-homecoming-history-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup> and became the school's official song in 1926.<sup id="cite_ref-Follow-up_on_the_news.3B_Song_out_of_tune_with_the_times_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Follow-up_on_the_news.3B_Song_out_of_tune_with_the_times-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup> The song was retitled to &quot;Alma Mater&quot; in the 1980s when its lyrics were changed to refer to women as well as men.<sup id="cite_ref-rscl_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rscl-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Seal">Seal</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dartmouth_College&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Seal">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Seal_of_Dartmouth_College" title="Seal of Dartmouth College">Seal of Dartmouth College</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Seal_of_Dartmouth_College.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/af/Seal_of_Dartmouth_College.png/170px-Seal_of_Dartmouth_College.png" width="170" height="193" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/a/af/Seal_of_Dartmouth_College.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/a/af/Seal_of_Dartmouth_College.png 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Seal_of_Dartmouth_College.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Seal of Dartmouth College
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Dartmouth's 1769 royal charter required the creation of a <a href="/wiki/Seal_(device)" title="Seal (device)" class="mw-redirect">seal</a> for use on official documents and diplomas.<sup id="cite_ref-charter_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charter-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> The College's founder <a href="/wiki/Eleazar_Wheelock" title="Eleazar Wheelock">Eleazar Wheelock</a> designed a seal for his college bearing a striking resemblance to the seal of the <a href="/wiki/Society_for_the_Propagation_of_the_Gospel" title="Society for the Propagation of the Gospel" class="mw-redirect">Society for the Propagation of the Gospel</a>, a missionary society founded in London in 1701, in order to maintain the illusion that his college was more for mission work than for higher education.<sup id="cite_ref-good_161-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-good-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup> Engraved by a Boston silversmith, the seal was ready by Commencement of 1773. The trustees officially accepted the seal on August 25, 1773, describing it as:</p> 
     <blockquote class="templatequote"> 
      <div class="Bug6200">
       An Oval, circumscribed by a Line containing SIGILL: COL: DARTMUTH: NOV: HANT: IN AMERICA 1770. within projecting a Pine Grove on the Right, whence proceed Natives towards an Edifice two Storey on the left; which bears in a Label over the Grove these Words &quot;vox clamantis in deserto&quot; the whole supported by Religion on the Right and Justice on the Left, and bearing in a Triangle irradiate, with the Hebrew Words [El Shaddai], agreeable to the above Impression, be the common Seal under which to pass all Diplomas or Certificates of Degrees, and all other Affairs of Business of and concerning Dartmouth College.
       <sup id="cite_ref-collections_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-collections-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup>
      </div> 
     </blockquote> 
     <p>On October 28, 1926, the trustees affirmed the charter's reservation of the seal for official corporate documents alone.<sup id="cite_ref-good_161-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-good-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup> The College Publications Committee commissioned noted typographer <a href="/wiki/William_Addison_Dwiggins" title="William Addison Dwiggins">W. A. Dwiggins</a> to create a line drawing version of the seal in 1940 that saw widespread use. Dwiggins' design was modified during 1957 to change the date from &quot;1770&quot; to &quot;1769,&quot; to accord with the date of the College Charter. The trustees commissioned a new set of dies with a date of &quot;1769&quot; to replace the old dies, now badly worn after almost two hundred years of use.<sup id="cite_ref-good_161-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-good-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup> The 1957 design continues to be used under trademark number 2305032.<sup id="cite_ref-uspatent_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uspatent-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shield">Shield</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dartmouth_College&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Shield">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>On October 28, 1926, the Trustees approved a &quot;Dartmouth College Shield&quot; for general use. Artist and engraver W. Parke Johnson designed this emblem on the basis of the shield that is depicted at the center of the original seal. This design does not survive. On June 9, 1944 the trustees approved another <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a> based on the shield part of the seal, this one by Canadian artist and designer <a href="/wiki/Thoreau_MacDonald" title="Thoreau MacDonald">Thoreau MacDonald</a>. That design was used widely and, like Dwiggins' seal, had its date changed from &quot;1770&quot; to &quot;1769&quot; around 1958.<sup id="cite_ref-good_161-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-good-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup> That version continues to be used under trademark registration number 3112676 and others.<sup id="cite_ref-uspatent_167-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uspatent-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>College designer John Scotford made a stylized version of the shield during the 1960s, but it did not see the success of MacDonald's design.<sup id="cite_ref-A_Proposal_for_a_Heraldic_Coat_of_Arms_for_Dartmouth_College_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A_Proposal_for_a_Heraldic_Coat_of_Arms_for_Dartmouth_College-168"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup> The shield appears to have been used as the basis of the shield of <a href="/wiki/Dartmouth_Medical_School" title="Dartmouth Medical School" class="mw-redirect">Dartmouth Medical School</a>, and it has been reproduced in sizes as small as 20 micrometers across.<sup id="cite_ref-Nanometer_Pattern_Generation_System:_Dartmouth_Seal_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nanometer_Pattern_Generation_System:_Dartmouth_Seal-169"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup> The design has appeared on <a href="/wiki/Rudolph_Ruzicka" title="Rudolph Ruzicka">Rudolph Ruzicka</a>'s Bicentennial Medal (<a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Mint" title="Philadelphia Mint">Philadelphia Mint</a>, 1969) and elsewhere.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nickname.2C_symbol.2C_and_mascot">Nickname, symbol, and mascot</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dartmouth_College&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Nickname, symbol, and mascot">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Keggy_the_Keg.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Keggy_the_Keg.JPG/170px-Keggy_the_Keg.JPG" width="170" height="257" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Keggy_the_Keg.JPG/255px-Keggy_the_Keg.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Keggy_the_Keg.JPG/340px-Keggy_the_Keg.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Keggy_the_Keg.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Keggy posing on the Dartmouth College Green.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Dartmouth has never had an official mascot.<sup id="cite_ref-ad-green_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ad-green-170"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup> The nickname &quot;The Big Green,&quot; originating in the 1860s, is based on students' adoption of a shade of forest green (&quot;Dartmouth Green&quot;) as the school's official color in 1866.<sup id="cite_ref-greencolor_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greencolor-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-History-of-Dartmouth-Hanover_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History-of-Dartmouth-Hanover-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup> Beginning in the 1920s, the Dartmouth College athletic teams were known by their unofficial nickname &quot;the Indians,&quot; a moniker that probably originated among sports journalists.<sup id="cite_ref-ad-green_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ad-green-170"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup> This unofficial mascot and team name was used until the early 1970s, when its use came under criticism. In 1974, the Trustees declared the &quot;use of the [Indian] symbol in any form to be inconsistent with present institutional and academic objectives of the College in advancing Native American education.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-The_.27Big_Green.27_Nickname_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_.27Big_Green.27_Nickname-172"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup> Some alumni and students, as well as the conservative student newspaper, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dartmouth_Review" title="The Dartmouth Review">The Dartmouth Review</a></i>, have sought to return the Indian symbol to prominence,<sup id="cite_ref-Dartmouth_Indians:_The_New_Tradition_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dartmouth_Indians:_The_New_Tradition-173"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup> but no team has worn the symbol on its uniform in decades.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Banning_of_the_Indian_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Banning_of_the_Indian-174"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Various student initiatives have been undertaken to adopt a new mascot, but none has become &quot;official.&quot; One proposal devised by the College humor magazine the <i><a href="/wiki/Dartmouth_Jack-O-Lantern" title="Dartmouth Jack-O-Lantern">Dartmouth Jack-O-Lantern</a></i> was <a href="/wiki/Keggy_the_Keg" title="Keggy the Keg">Keggy the Keg</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Anthropomorphism" title="Anthropomorphism">anthropomorphic</a> beer keg who makes occasional appearances at College sporting events. Despite student enthusiasm for Keggy,<sup id="cite_ref-Straight_from_the_Tap:_the_men_behind_the_mascot_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Straight_from_the_Tap:_the_men_behind_the_mascot-175"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup> the mascot has only received approval from the student government.<sup id="cite_ref-thedartmouth4_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thedartmouth4-176"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup> In November 2006, student government attempted to revive the &quot;Dartmoose&quot; as a potential replacement amid renewed controversy surrounding the former Indian mascot.<sup id="cite_ref-First_SA_meeting_draws_crowd_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-First_SA_meeting_draws_crowd-177"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Alumni">Alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dartmouth_College&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Alumni">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dartmouth_College_alumni" title="List of Dartmouth College alumni">List of Dartmouth College alumni</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Dartmouth's alumni are known for their devotion to the College.<sup id="cite_ref-ihe-alum_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ihe-alum-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> Most start by giving to the Senior Class Gift. According to a 2008 article in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i>, Dartmouth graduates also earn higher median salaries at least 10&nbsp;years after graduation than alumni of any other American university surveyed.<sup id="cite_ref-Ivy_Leaguers.27_Big_Edge:_Starting_Pay_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ivy_Leaguers.27_Big_Edge:_Starting_Pay-178"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Mathew_Brady,_Portrait_of_Secretary_of_the_Treasury_Salmon_P._Chase,_officer_of_the_United_States_government_(1860%E2%80%931865,_full_version).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Mathew_Brady%2C_Portrait_of_Secretary_of_the_Treasury_Salmon_P._Chase%2C_officer_of_the_United_States_government_%281860%E2%80%931865%2C_full_version%29.jpg/220px-Mathew_Brady%2C_Portrait_of_Secretary_of_the_Treasury_Salmon_P._Chase%2C_officer_of_the_United_States_government_%281860%E2%80%931865%2C_full_version%29.jpg" width="220" height="248" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Mathew_Brady%2C_Portrait_of_Secretary_of_the_Treasury_Salmon_P._Chase%2C_officer_of_the_United_States_government_%281860%E2%80%931865%2C_full_version%29.jpg/330px-Mathew_Brady%2C_Portrait_of_Secretary_of_the_Treasury_Salmon_P._Chase%2C_officer_of_the_United_States_government_%281860%E2%80%931865%2C_full_version%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Mathew_Brady%2C_Portrait_of_Secretary_of_the_Treasury_Salmon_P._Chase%2C_officer_of_the_United_States_government_%281860%E2%80%931865%2C_full_version%29.jpg/440px-Mathew_Brady%2C_Portrait_of_Secretary_of_the_Treasury_Salmon_P._Chase%2C_officer_of_the_United_States_government_%281860%E2%80%931865%2C_full_version%29.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Mathew_Brady,_Portrait_of_Secretary_of_the_Treasury_Salmon_P._Chase,_officer_of_the_United_States_government_(1860%E2%80%931865,_full_version).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Salmon_P._Chase" title="Salmon P. Chase">Salmon P. Chase</a>, class of 1826, was an American politician: Senator from Ohio, Governor of Ohio, Secretary of the Treasury under Abraham Lincoln, and Chief Justice of the Supreme Court.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>By 2008, Dartmouth had graduated 238 classes of students and has over 60,000 living alumni in a variety of fields.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Alumni_Constitution.2C_in_Brief_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Alumni_Constitution.2C_in_Brief-179"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Nelson_Rockefeller" title="Nelson Rockefeller">Nelson A. Rockefeller</a>, 41st <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States" title="Vice President of the United States">Vice President of the United States</a> and 49th <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_New_York" title="Governor of New York">Governor of New York</a>, graduated cum laude from Dartmouth with a degree in economics in 1930. Over 164 Dartmouth graduates have served in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">United States Senate</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">United States House of Representatives</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-dartmouthclub_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dartmouthclub-180"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup> such as Massachusetts statesman <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Webster" title="Daniel Webster">Daniel Webster</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dartmouthclub_180-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dartmouthclub-180"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup> Cabinet members of American presidents include Attorney General <a href="/wiki/Amos_T._Akerman" title="Amos T. Akerman">Amos T. Akerman</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Amos_T._Akerman_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amos_T._Akerman-181"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup> Secretary of Defense <a href="/wiki/James_V._Forrestal" title="James V. Forrestal" class="mw-redirect">James V. Forrestal</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-James_V._Forrestal_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-James_V._Forrestal-182"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup> Secretary of Labor <a href="/wiki/Robert_Reich" title="Robert Reich">Robert Reich</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-dartmouth5_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dartmouth5-183"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup> former Secretary of the Treasury <a href="/wiki/Henry_Paulson" title="Henry Paulson">Henry Paulson</a>, and former Secretary of the Treasury <a href="/wiki/Timothy_Geithner" title="Timothy Geithner">Timothy Geithner</a>. <a href="/wiki/C._Everett_Koop" title="C. Everett Koop">C. Everett Koop</a> was the <a href="/wiki/Surgeon_General_of_the_United_States" title="Surgeon General of the United States">Surgeon General of the United States</a> under President Ronald Reagan.<sup id="cite_ref-C._Everett_Koop_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C._Everett_Koop-184"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup> Two Dartmouth alumni have served as justices on the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">Supreme Court of the United States</a>: <a href="/wiki/Salmon_P._Chase" title="Salmon P. Chase">Salmon P. Chase</a> and <a href="/wiki/Levi_Woodbury" title="Levi Woodbury">Levi Woodbury</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Salmon_P._Chase_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Salmon_P._Chase-185"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Levi_Woodbury_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levi_Woodbury-186"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup> Eugene Norman Veasey (class of 1954) served as the Chief Justice of Delaware.</p> 
     <p>In literature and journalism, Dartmouth has produced nine <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winners: Thomas M. Burton,<sup id="cite_ref-Wall_Street.2C_Aneurysms_and_Explanatory_Writing:_An_Interview_With_Thomas_Burton_.2771_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wall_Street.2C_Aneurysms_and_Explanatory_Writing:_An_Interview_With_Thomas_Burton_.2771-187"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Richard_Eberhart" title="Richard Eberhart">Richard Eberhart</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Richard_Eberhart_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Richard_Eberhart-188"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Frost" title="Robert Frost">Robert Frost</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Virginia_graduate_student_discovers_new_Frost_poem_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Virginia_graduate_student_discovers_new_Frost_poem-189"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Paul_Gigot" title="Paul Gigot">Paul Gigot</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Paul_Gigot_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paul_Gigot-190"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jake_Hooker_(journalist)" title="Jake Hooker (journalist)">Jake Hooker</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-More_GreenNews_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-More_GreenNews-191"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Jaquiss" title="Nigel Jaquiss">Nigel Jaquiss</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-The_Pulitzer_Prize_Winners_2005_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Pulitzer_Prize_Winners_2005-192"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Martin_J._Sherwin" title="Martin J. Sherwin">Martin J. Sherwin</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-History6_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History6-193"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/David_K._Shipler" title="David K. Shipler">David K. Shipler</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Six_to_receive_Social_Justice_Awards_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Six_to_receive_Social_Justice_Awards-194"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup> and Joseph Rago.<sup id="cite_ref-WSJ.27s_Rago_Wins_Pulitzer_Prize_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ.27s_Rago_Wins_Pulitzer_Prize-195"><span>[</span>195<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Other authors and media personalities include ABC Senior White House correspondent <a href="/wiki/Jake_Tapper" title="Jake Tapper">Jake Tapper</a>, novelist/screenwriter <a href="/wiki/Budd_Schulberg" title="Budd Schulberg">Budd Schulberg</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-dartmouth7_196-0" class="reference"><a id="cite_ref-About_Dinesh_D.27Souza_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_Dinesh_D.27Souza-197"><span>[</span>197<span>]</span></a></sup> radio talk show host <a href="/wiki/Laura_Ingraham" title="Laura Ingraham">Laura Ingraham</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Ingraham_.2785_to_speak_on_election_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ingraham_.2785_to_speak_on_election-198"><span>[</span>198<span>]</span></a></sup> commentator <a href="/wiki/Mort_Kondracke" title="Mort Kondracke" class="mw-redirect">Mort Kondracke</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Mort_Kondracke_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mort_Kondracke-199"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup> and journalist <a href="/wiki/James_Panero" title="James Panero">James Panero</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-James_Panero_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-James_Panero-200"><span>[</span>200<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Norman_Maclean" title="Norman Maclean">Norman Maclean</a>, a former professor at the University of Chicago<sup id="cite_ref-Professor.2C_Outdoorsman.2C_Now_a_Novelist.E2.80.94Norman_Maclean_.27Finds_Life_Again.27_at_73_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Professor.2C_Outdoorsman.2C_Now_a_Novelist.E2.80.94Norman_Maclean_.27Finds_Life_Again.27_at_73-201"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup> and author of <i>A River Runs Through It and Other Stories</i>, graduated from Dartmouth in 1924.<sup id="cite_ref-And_to_Think_That_It_Happened_at_Dartmouth_202-0" class="reference"><a Seuss">Dr. Seuss</a>, was a member of the class of 1925.<sup id="cite_ref-Who.27s_Who_.26_What.27s_What_in_the_Books_of_Dr._Seuss_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Who.27s_Who_.26_What.27s_What_in_the_Books_of_Dr._Seuss-203"><span>[</span>203<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the area of religion and theology, Dartmouth alumni include priests and ministers <a href="/wiki/Ebenezer_Porter" title="Ebenezer Porter">Ebenezer Porter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Clarkson_Gibbs" title="Jonathan Clarkson Gibbs">Jonathan Clarkson Gibbs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caleb_Sprague_Henry" title="Caleb Sprague Henry">Caleb Sprague Henry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Whipple_Jenks" title="Arthur Whipple Jenks">Arthur Whipple Jenks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Spalding" title="Solomon Spalding">Solomon Spalding</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Tracy" title="Joseph Tracy">Joseph Tracy</a>; and rabbis <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Meyer" title="Marshall Meyer">Marshall Meyer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Resnicoff" title="Arnold Resnicoff">Arnold Resnicoff</a>, and <a href="/wiki/David_E._Stern" title="David E. Stern">David E. Stern</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CalebHenry_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CalebHenry-204"><span>[</span>204<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SolSpaldingAlum_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SolSpaldingAlum-205"><span>[</span>205<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Bibliography_of_Vermont:_Or.2C_A_List_of_Books_and_Pamphlets_Relating_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Bibliography_of_Vermont:_Or.2C_A_List_of_Books_and_Pamphlets_Relating-206"><span>[</span>206<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RabiStern_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RabiStern-207"><span>[</span>207<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Alum-Resnicoff_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alum-Resnicoff-208"><span>[</span>208<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hyrum_Smith" title="Hyrum Smith">Hyrum Smith</a>, brother of Mormon Prophet <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Smith" title="Joseph Smith">Joseph Smith</a> also attended the college in his teens. He was Patriarch of the <a href="/wiki/LDS_Church" title="LDS Church" class="mw-redirect">LDS Church</a>.</p> 
     <p>Dartmouth alumni in academia include <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Kauffman" title="Stuart Kauffman">Stuart Kauffman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Weeks_(mathematician)" title="Jeffrey Weeks (mathematician)">Jeffrey Weeks</a>, both recipients of <a href="/wiki/MacArthur_Fellows_Program" title="MacArthur Fellows Program">MacArthur Fellowships</a> (commonly called &quot;genius grants&quot;).<sup id="cite_ref-Stuart_Kauffman_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stuart_Kauffman-209"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Vita_for_Dr._Jeffrey_Weeks_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vita_for_Dr._Jeffrey_Weeks-210"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup> Dartmouth has also graduated three <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a> winners: <a href="/wiki/Owen_Chamberlain" title="Owen Chamberlain">Owen Chamberlain</a> (<a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics" title="Nobel Prize in Physics">Physics</a>, 1959),<sup id="cite_ref-Owen_Chamberlain_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Owen_Chamberlain-211"><span>[</span>211<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/K._Barry_Sharpless" title="K. Barry Sharpless" class="mw-redirect">K. Barry Sharpless</a> (<a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Chemistry" title="Nobel Prize in Chemistry">Chemistry</a>, 2001),<sup id="cite_ref-K._Berry_Sharpless_curriculum_vitae_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-K._Berry_Sharpless_curriculum_vitae-212"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/George_Davis_Snell" title="George Davis Snell">George Davis Snell</a> (<a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physiology_or_Medicine" title="Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine">Physiology or Medicine</a>, 1980).<sup id="cite_ref-George_Davis_Snell_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-George_Davis_Snell-213"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup> Educators include the current chancellor of the University of California, San Diego <a href="/wiki/Marye_Anne_Fox" title="Marye Anne Fox">Marye Anne Fox</a> (PhD. in Chemistry, 1974),<sup id="cite_ref-dartmouth8_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dartmouth8-214"><span>[</span>214<span>]</span></a></sup> founding president of <a href="/wiki/Vassar_College" title="Vassar College">Vassar College</a> <a href="/wiki/Milo_Parker_Jewett" title="Milo Parker Jewett">Milo Parker Jewett</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Double_Play:_Women.27s_Education_and_Anti-Slavery_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Double_Play:_Women.27s_Education_and_Anti-Slavery-215"><span>[</span>215<span>]</span></a></sup> founder and first president of Bates College <a href="/wiki/Oren_B._Cheney" title="Oren B. Cheney">Oren B. Cheney</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Oren_B._Cheney_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oren_B._Cheney-216"><span>[</span>216<span>]</span></a></sup> founder and first president of Kenyon College <a href="/wiki/Philander_Chase" title="Philander Chase">Philander Chase</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Philander_Chase_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Philander_Chase-217"><span>[</span>217<span>]</span></a></sup> first professor of Wabash College <a href="/wiki/Caleb_Mills" title="Caleb Mills">Caleb Mills</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Wabash_College:_The_First_Hundred_Years.2C_1832.E2.80.931932_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wabash_College:_The_First_Hundred_Years.2C_1832.E2.80.931932-218"><span>[</span>218<span>]</span></a></sup> and former president of Union College <a href="/wiki/Charles_Augustus_Aiken" title="Charles Augustus Aiken">Charles Augustus Aiken</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Woodward_Succession:_A_Brief_History_of_the_Dartmouth_College_Library.2C_1769.E2.80.932002_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Woodward_Succession:_A_Brief_History_of_the_Dartmouth_College_Library.2C_1769.E2.80.932002-219"><span>[</span>219<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Past_Presidents_of_Union_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Past_Presidents_of_Union-220"><span>[</span>220<span>]</span></a></sup> Nine of Dartmouth's 17 presidents were alumni of the College.<sup id="cite_ref-dart-pres_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dart-pres-221"><span>[</span>221<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

     <p>A number of Dartmouth alumni have found success in professional sports. In baseball, Dartmouth alumni include All-Star and three-time <a href="/wiki/Gold_Glove" title="Gold Glove" class="mw-redirect">Gold Glove</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Brad_Ausmus" title="Brad Ausmus">Brad Ausmus</a><sup id="cite_ref-Ausmus_.2791_produces_Gold_Gloves_and_success_for_Astros_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ausmus_.2791_produces_Gold_Gloves_and_success_for_Astros-235"><span>[</span>235<span>]</span></a></sup> and All-Star <a href="/wiki/Mike_Remlinger" title="Mike Remlinger">Mike Remlinger</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Mike_Remlinger_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mike_Remlinger-236"><span>[</span>236<span>]</span></a></sup> Professional football players include former Miami Dolphins quarterback <a href="/wiki/Jay_Fiedler" title="Jay Fiedler">Jay Fiedler</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Dolphins_still_winning.2C_Jay_Fiedler_.2794_still_standing_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dolphins_still_winning.2C_Jay_Fiedler_.2794_still_standing-237"><span>[</span>237<span>]</span></a></sup> linebacker <a href="/wiki/Reggie_Williams_(linebacker)" title="Reggie Williams (linebacker)">Reggie Williams</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-2004_Greater_Flint_Afro-American_Hall_of_Fame:_Reggie_Williams_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2004_Greater_Flint_Afro-American_Hall_of_Fame:_Reggie_Williams-238"><span>[</span>238<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dartmouthsports_239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dartmouthsports-239"><span>[</span>239<span>]</span></a></sup> three-time Pro Bowler <a href="/wiki/Nick_Lowery" title="Nick Lowery">Nick Lowery</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Football_star_Nick_Lowery_to_discuss_community_service_Oct._29_at_Dartmouth_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Football_star_Nick_Lowery_to_discuss_community_service_Oct._29_at_Dartmouth-240"><span>[</span>240<span>]</span></a></sup> quarterback <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Kemp" title="Jeff Kemp">Jeff Kemp</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Jeff_Kemp_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jeff_Kemp-241"><span>[</span>241<span>]</span></a></sup> and Tennessee Titans tight end <a href="/wiki/Casey_Cramer" title="Casey Cramer">Casey Cramer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Sports_Roundup_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sports_Roundup-242"><span>[</span>242<span>]</span></a></sup> Dartmouth has also produced a number of Olympic competitors. <a href="/wiki/Adam_Nelson" title="Adam Nelson">Adam Nelson</a> won the silver medal in the shotput in the <a href="/wiki/2000_Sydney_Olympics" title="2000 Sydney Olympics" class="mw-redirect">2000 Sydney Olympics</a> and the gold medal at the <a href="/wiki/2004_Athens_Olympics" title="2004 Athens Olympics" class="mw-redirect">2004 Athens Olympics</a> to go along with his gold medal in the <a href="/wiki/2005_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="2005 World Championships in Athletics">2005 World Championships in Athletics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">Helsinki</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-usatf.org_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usatf.org-243"><span>[</span>243<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kristin_King" title="Kristin King">Kristin King</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Parsons" title="Sarah Parsons">Sarah Parsons</a> were members of the United States' 2006 bronze medal-winning ice hockey team.<sup id="cite_ref-thed-olymp-ath_244-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thed-olymp-ath-244"><span>[</span>244<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sports:_One_on_One_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sports:_One_on_One-245"><span>[</span>245<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cherie_Piper" title="Cherie Piper">Cherie Piper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gillian_Apps" title="Gillian Apps">Gillian Apps</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Katie_Weatherston" title="Katie Weatherston">Katie Weatherston</a> were among Canada's ice hockey gold medalists in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-Cherie_Piper_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cherie_Piper-246"><span>[</span>246<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gillian_Apps_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gillian_Apps-247"><span>[</span>247<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Katie_Weatherston_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Katie_Weatherston-248"><span>[</span>248<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Dick_Durrance" title="Dick Durrance">Dick Durrance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tim_Caldwell_(skier)" title="Tim Caldwell (skier)">Tim Caldwell</a> competed for the United States in skiing in the 1936 and 1976 Winter Olympics, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-Dick_Durrance.2C_America.27s_Champion_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dick_Durrance.2C_America.27s_Champion-249"><span>[</span>249<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dartmouth-pdf_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dartmouth-pdf-250"><span>[</span>250<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Shaw_(athlete)" title="Arthur Shaw (athlete)">Arthur Shaw</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-bgtf_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bgtf-251"><span>[</span>251<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Earl_Thompson_(athlete)" title="Earl Thompson (athlete)" class="mw-redirect">Earl Thompson</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-NCAA_Champions_from_Dartmouth_College_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NCAA_Champions_from_Dartmouth_College-252"><span>[</span>252<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Myers" title="Edwin Myers">Edwin Myers</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-bgtf_251-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bgtf-251"><span>[</span>251<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Marc_Wright" title="Marc Wright">Marc Wright</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-bgtf_251-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bgtf-251"><span>[</span>251<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Adam_Nelson" title="Adam Nelson">Adam Nelson</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-usatf.org_243-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usatf.org-243"><span>[</span>243<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gerry_Ashworth" title="Gerry Ashworth">Gerry Ashworth</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-bgtf_251-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bgtf-251"><span>[</span>251<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Vilhj%C3%A1lmur_Einarsson" title="Vilhj&aacute;lmur Einarsson">Vilhj&aacute;lmur Einarsson</a><sup id="cite_ref-bgtf_251-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bgtf-251"><span>[</span>251<span>]</span></a></sup> have all won medals in track and field events. Former heavyweight <a href="/wiki/Rowing_(sport)" title="Rowing (sport)">rower</a> <a href="/wiki/Dominic_Seiterle" title="Dominic Seiterle">Dominic Seiterle</a> is a member of the Canadian national rowing team and won a gold medal at the <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">2008 Summer Olympics</a> in the men's <a href="/wiki/Eight_(rowing)" title="Eight (rowing)">8+</a> event.<sup id="cite_ref-Gold_in_Men.27s_Eight.2C_Bronze_in_Women.27s_Double.2C_Men.27s_Four_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gold_in_Men.27s_Eight.2C_Bronze_in_Women.27s_Double.2C_Men.27s_Four-253"><span>[</span>253<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alumni_income">Alumni income</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dartmouth_College&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Alumni income">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>According to Payscale, Dartmouth College alums have among the highest average starting salaries ($58,200) in the United States, as well as the second highest average income ten years after graduation ($123,000), placing after Harvey Mudd College and tying with Princeton University.<sup id="cite_ref-payscale_254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-payscale-254"><span>[</span>254<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Top_Colleges_For_Getting_Rich_255-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top_Colleges_For_Getting_Rich-255"><span>[</span>255<span>]</span></a></sup> Most recently in 2010, Payscale also ranked Dartmouth first in producing CEOs of for-profit companies, out of all undergraduate programs at United States universities.<sup id="cite_ref-Most_Popular_Colleges_for_For-Profit_CEOs_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Most_Popular_Colleges_for_For-Profit_CEOs-256"><span>[</span>256<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dartmouth_College&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>Dartmouth College has appeared in or been referenced by a number of popular media. Most notably, the 1978 comedy film <i><a href="/wiki/National_Lampoon%27s_Animal_House" title="National Lampoon's Animal House">National Lampoon's Animal House</a></i> was co-written by <a href="/wiki/Chris_Miller_(writer)" title="Chris Miller (writer)">Chris Miller</a> '63, and is based loosely on a series of stories he wrote about his fraternity days at Dartmouth. In a CNN interview, <a href="/wiki/John_Landis" title="John Landis">John Landis</a> said the movie was &quot;based on Chris Miller's real fraternity at Dartmouth&quot;, <a href="/wiki/Dartmouth_College_Greek_organizations#Alpha_Delta" title="Dartmouth College Greek organizations">Alpha Delta Phi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Interview_with_John_Landis_257-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Interview_with_John_Landis-257"><span>[</span>257<span>]</span></a></sup> Dartmouth's <a href="#Traditions">Winter Carnival</a> tradition was the subject of the 1939 film <i>Winter Carnival</i> starring <a href="/wiki/Ann_Sheridan" title="Ann Sheridan">Ann Sheridan</a> and written by <a href="/wiki/Budd_Schulberg" title="Budd Schulberg">Budd Schulberg</a> '36 and <a href="/wiki/F._Scott_Fitzgerald" title="F. Scott Fitzgerald">F. Scott Fitzgerald</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tdr-wc_155-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tdr-wc-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
